5054      * types and values of the {@code N} parameters and arguments at the folding
5055      * position. {@code Z}/{@code z} and {@code B}/{@code b} represent the types
5056      * and values of the {@code target} parameters and arguments that precede and
5057      * follow the folded parameters and arguments starting at {@code pos},
5058      * respectively.
5059      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
5060      * // there are N arguments in A...
5061      * T target(Z..., V, A[N]..., B...);
5062      * V combiner(A...);
5063      * T adapter(Z... z, A... a, B... b) {
5064      *   V v = combiner(a...);
5065      *   return target(z..., v, a..., b...);
5066      * }
5067      * // and if the combiner has a void return:
5068      * T target2(Z..., A[N]..., B...);
5069      * void combiner2(A...);
5070      * T adapter2(Z... z, A... a, B... b) {
5071      *   combiner2(a...);
5072      *   return target2(z..., a..., b...);
5073      * }
5074      * }</pre></blockquote>
5075      * <p>
5076      * <em>Note:</em> The resulting adapter is never a {@linkplain MethodHandle#asVarargsCollector
5077      * variable-arity method handle}, even if the original target method handle was.
5078      *
5079      * @param target the method handle to invoke after arguments are combined
5080      * @param pos the position at which to start folding and at which to insert the folding result; if this is {@code
5081      *            0}, the effect is the same as for {@link #foldArguments(MethodHandle, MethodHandle)}.
5082      * @param combiner method handle to call initially on the incoming arguments
5083      * @return method handle which incorporates the specified argument folding logic
5084      * @throws NullPointerException if either argument is null
5085      * @throws IllegalArgumentException if either of the following two conditions holds:
5086      *          (1) {@code combiner}'s return type is non-{@code void} and not the same as the argument type at position
5087      *              {@code pos} of the target signature;
5088      *          (2) the {@code N} argument types at position {@code pos} of the target signature (skipping one matching
5089      *              the {@code combiner}'s return type) are not identical with the argument types of {@code combiner}.
5090      *
5091      * @see #foldArguments(MethodHandle, MethodHandle)
5092      * @since 9
5093      */
5094     public static MethodHandle foldArguments(MethodHandle target, int pos, MethodHandle combiner) {
5095         MethodType targetType = target.type();
5096         MethodType combinerType = combiner.type();
5097         Class<?> rtype = foldArgumentChecks(pos, targetType, combinerType);
5098         BoundMethodHandle result = target.rebind();
5099         boolean dropResult = rtype == void.class;
5100         LambdaForm lform = result.editor().foldArgumentsForm(1 + pos, dropResult, combinerType.basicType());
5101         MethodType newType = targetType;
5102         if (!dropResult) {
5103             newType = newType.dropParameterTypes(pos, pos + 1);
5104         }
5105         result = result.copyWithExtendL(newType, lform, combiner);
5106         return result;
5107     }
5108 
5109     private static Class<?> foldArgumentChecks(int foldPos, MethodType targetType, MethodType combinerType) {
5110         int foldArgs   = combinerType.parameterCount();
5111         Class<?> rtype = combinerType.returnType();
5112         int foldVals = rtype == void.class ? 0 : 1;
5113         int afterInsertPos = foldPos + foldVals;
5114         boolean ok = (targetType.parameterCount() >= afterInsertPos + foldArgs);
5115         if (ok) {
5116             for (int i = 0; i < foldArgs; i++) {
5117                 if (combinerType.parameterType(i) != targetType.parameterType(i + afterInsertPos)) {
5118                     ok = false;
5119                     break;
5120                 }
5121             }
5122         }
5123         if (ok && foldVals != 0 && combinerType.returnType() != targetType.parameterType(foldPos))
5124             ok = false;
5125         if (!ok)
5126             throw misMatchedTypes("target and combiner types", targetType, combinerType);
5127         return rtype;
5128     }
5129 
5130     /**
5131      * Adapts a target method handle by pre-processing some of its arguments, then calling the target with the result
5132      * of the pre-processing replacing the argument at the given position.
5133      *
5134      * @param target the method handle to invoke after arguments are combined
5135      * @param position the position at which to start folding and at which to insert the folding result; if this is {@code
5136      *            0}, the effect is the same as for {@link #foldArguments(MethodHandle, MethodHandle)}.
5137      * @param combiner method handle to call initially on the incoming arguments
5138      * @param argPositions indexes of the target to pick arguments sent to the combiner from
5139      * @return method handle which incorporates the specified argument folding logic
5140      * @throws NullPointerException if either argument is null
5141      * @throws IllegalArgumentException if either of the following two conditions holds:
5142      *          (1) {@code combiner}'s return type is not the same as the argument type at position
5143      *              {@code pos} of the target signature;
5144      *          (2) the {@code N} argument types at positions {@code argPositions[1...N]} of the target signature are
5145      *              not identical with the argument types of {@code combiner}.
5146      */
5147     /*non-public*/
5148     static MethodHandle filterArgumentsWithCombiner(MethodHandle target, int position, MethodHandle combiner, int ... argPositions) {
5149         return argumentsWithCombiner(true, target, position, combiner, argPositions);
5150     }
5151 
5152     /**
5153      * Adapts a target method handle by pre-processing some of its arguments, calling the target with the result of
5154      * the pre-processing inserted into the original sequence of arguments at the given position.
5155      *
5156      * @param target the method handle to invoke after arguments are combined
5157      * @param position the position at which to start folding and at which to insert the folding result; if this is {@code
5158      *            0}, the effect is the same as for {@link #foldArguments(MethodHandle, MethodHandle)}.
5159      * @param combiner method handle to call initially on the incoming arguments
5160      * @param argPositions indexes of the target to pick arguments sent to the combiner from
5161      * @return method handle which incorporates the specified argument folding logic
5162      * @throws NullPointerException if either argument is null
5163      * @throws IllegalArgumentException if either of the following two conditions holds:
5164      *          (1) {@code combiner}'s return type is non-{@code void} and not the same as the argument type at position
5165      *              {@code pos} of the target signature;
5166      *          (2) the {@code N} argument types at positions {@code argPositions[1...N]} of the target signature
5167      *              (skipping {@code position} where the {@code combiner}'s return will be folded in) are not identical
5168      *              with the argument types of {@code combiner}.
5169      */
5170     /*non-public*/
5171     static MethodHandle foldArgumentsWithCombiner(MethodHandle target, int position, MethodHandle combiner, int ... argPositions) {
5172         return argumentsWithCombiner(false, target, position, combiner, argPositions);
5173     }
5174 
5175     private static MethodHandle argumentsWithCombiner(boolean filter, MethodHandle target, int position, MethodHandle combiner, int ... argPositions) {
5176         MethodType targetType = target.type();
5177         MethodType combinerType = combiner.type();
5178         Class<?> rtype = argumentsWithCombinerChecks(position, filter, targetType, combinerType, argPositions);
5179         BoundMethodHandle result = target.rebind();
5180 
5181         MethodType newType = targetType;
5182         LambdaForm lform;
5183         if (filter) {
5184             lform = result.editor().filterArgumentsForm(1 + position, combinerType.basicType(), argPositions);
5185         } else {
5186             boolean dropResult = rtype == void.class;
5187             lform = result.editor().foldArgumentsForm(1 + position, dropResult, combinerType.basicType(), argPositions);
5188             if (!dropResult) {
5189                 newType = newType.dropParameterTypes(position, position + 1);
5190             }
5191         }
5192         result = result.copyWithExtendL(newType, lform, combiner);
5193         return result;
5194     }
5195 
5196     private static Class<?> argumentsWithCombinerChecks(int position, boolean filter, MethodType targetType, MethodType combinerType, int ... argPos) {
5197         int combinerArgs = combinerType.parameterCount();
5198         if (argPos.length != combinerArgs) {
5199             throw newIllegalArgumentException("combiner and argument map must be equal size", combinerType, argPos.length);
5200         }
5201         Class<?> rtype = combinerType.returnType();
5202 
5203         for (int i = 0; i < combinerArgs; i++) {
5204             int arg = argPos[i];
5205             if (arg < 0 || arg > targetType.parameterCount()) {
5206                 throw newIllegalArgumentException("arg outside of target parameterRange", targetType, arg);
5207             }
5208             if (combinerType.parameterType(i) != targetType.parameterType(arg)) {
5209                 throw newIllegalArgumentException("target argument type at position " + arg
5210                         + " must match combiner argument type at index " + i + ": " + targetType
5211                         + " -> " + combinerType + ", map: " + Arrays.toString(argPos));
5212             }
5213         }
5214         if (filter && combinerType.returnType() != targetType.parameterType(position)) {
5215             throw misMatchedTypes("target and combiner types", targetType, combinerType);
5216         }
5217         return rtype;
5218     }
5219 
5220     /**
5221      * Makes a method handle which adapts a target method handle,
5222      * by guarding it with a test, a boolean-valued method handle.
5223      * If the guard fails, a fallback handle is called instead.
5224      * All three method handles must have the same corresponding
5225      * argument and return types, except that the return type
5226      * of the test must be boolean, and the test is allowed
5227      * to have fewer arguments than the other two method handles.
5228      * <p>
5229      * Here is pseudocode for the resulting adapter. In the code, {@code T}
5230      * represents the uniform result type of the three involved handles;
5231      * {@code A}/{@code a}, the types and values of the {@code target}
5232      * parameters and arguments that are consumed by the {@code test}; and
5233      * {@code B}/{@code b}, those types and values of the {@code target}
5234      * parameters and arguments that are not consumed by the {@code test}.
5235      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
5236      * boolean test(A...);
5237      * T target(A...,B...);
5238      * T fallback(A...,B...);
5239      * T adapter(A... a,B... b) {
5240      *   if (test(a...))
5241      *     return target(a..., b...);
5242      *   else
5243      *     return fallback(a..., b...);
5244      * }
5245      * }</pre></blockquote>
5246      * Note that the test arguments ({@code a...} in the pseudocode) cannot
5247      * be modified by execution of the test, and so are passed unchanged
5248      * from the caller to the target or fallback as appropriate.
5249      * @param test method handle used for test, must return boolean
5250      * @param target method handle to call if test passes
5251      * @param fallback method handle to call if test fails
5252      * @return method handle which incorporates the specified if/then/else logic
5253      * @throws NullPointerException if any argument is null
5254      * @throws IllegalArgumentException if {@code test} does not return boolean,
5255      *          or if all three method types do not match (with the return
5256      *          type of {@code test} changed to match that of the target).
5257      */
5258     public static MethodHandle guardWithTest(MethodHandle test,
5259                                MethodHandle target,
5260                                MethodHandle fallback) {
5261         MethodType gtype = test.type();
5262         MethodType ttype = target.type();
5263         MethodType ftype = fallback.type();
5264         if (!ttype.equals(ftype))
5265             throw misMatchedTypes("target and fallback types", ttype, ftype);
5266         if (gtype.returnType() != boolean.class)
5267             throw newIllegalArgumentException("guard type is not a predicate "+gtype);
5268         List<Class<?>> targs = ttype.parameterList();
5269         test = dropArgumentsToMatch(test, 0, targs, 0, true);
5270         if (test == null) {
5271             throw misMatchedTypes("target and test types", ttype, gtype);
5272         }
5273         return MethodHandleImpl.makeGuardWithTest(test, target, fallback);
5274     }
5275 
5276     static <T> RuntimeException misMatchedTypes(String what, T t1, T t2) {
5277         return newIllegalArgumentException(what + " must match: " + t1 + " != " + t2);
5278     }
5279 
5280     /**
5281      * Makes a method handle which adapts a target method handle,
5282      * by running it inside an exception handler.
5283      * If the target returns normally, the adapter returns that value.
5284      * If an exception matching the specified type is thrown, the fallback
5285      * handle is called instead on the exception, plus the original arguments.
5286      * <p>
5287      * The target and handler must have the same corresponding
5288      * argument and return types, except that handler may omit trailing arguments
5289      * (similarly to the predicate in {@link #guardWithTest guardWithTest}).
5290      * Also, the handler must have an extra leading parameter of {@code exType} or a supertype.
5291      * <p>
5292      * Here is pseudocode for the resulting adapter. In the code, {@code T}
5293      * represents the return type of the {@code target} and {@code handler},
5294      * and correspondingly that of the resulting adapter; {@code A}/{@code a},
5295      * the types and values of arguments to the resulting handle consumed by
5296      * {@code handler}; and {@code B}/{@code b}, those of arguments to the
5297      * resulting handle discarded by {@code handler}.
5298      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
5299      * T target(A..., B...);
5300      * T handler(ExType, A...);
5301      * T adapter(A... a, B... b) {
5302      *   try {
5303      *     return target(a..., b...);
5304      *   } catch (ExType ex) {
5305      *     return handler(ex, a...);
5306      *   }
5307      * }
5308      * }</pre></blockquote>
5309      * Note that the saved arguments ({@code a...} in the pseudocode) cannot
5310      * be modified by execution of the target, and so are passed unchanged
5311      * from the caller to the handler, if the handler is invoked.
5312      * <p>
5313      * The target and handler must return the same type, even if the handler
5314      * always throws.  (This might happen, for instance, because the handler
5315      * is simulating a {@code finally} clause).
5316      * To create such a throwing handler, compose the handler creation logic
5317      * with {@link #throwException throwException},
5318      * in order to create a method handle of the correct return type.
5319      * @param target method handle to call
5320      * @param exType the type of exception which the handler will catch
5321      * @param handler method handle to call if a matching exception is thrown
5322      * @return method handle which incorporates the specified try/catch logic
5323      * @throws NullPointerException if any argument is null
5324      * @throws IllegalArgumentException if {@code handler} does not accept
5325      *          the given exception type, or if the method handle types do
5326      *          not match in their return types and their
5327      *          corresponding parameters
5328      * @see MethodHandles#tryFinally(MethodHandle, MethodHandle)
5329      */
5330     public static MethodHandle catchException(MethodHandle target,
5331                                 Class<? extends Throwable> exType,
5332                                 MethodHandle handler) {
5333         MethodType ttype = target.type();
5334         MethodType htype = handler.type();
5335         if (!Throwable.class.isAssignableFrom(exType))
5336             throw new ClassCastException(exType.getName());
5337         if (htype.parameterCount() < 1 ||
5338             !htype.parameterType(0).isAssignableFrom(exType))
5339             throw newIllegalArgumentException("handler does not accept exception type "+exType);
5340         if (htype.returnType() != ttype.returnType())
5341             throw misMatchedTypes("target and handler return types", ttype, htype);
5342         handler = dropArgumentsToMatch(handler, 1, ttype.parameterList(), 0, true);
5343         if (handler == null) {
5344             throw misMatchedTypes("target and handler types", ttype, htype);
5345         }
5346         return MethodHandleImpl.makeGuardWithCatch(target, exType, handler);
5347     }
5348 
5349     /**
5350      * Produces a method handle which will throw exceptions of the given {@code exType}.
5351      * The method handle will accept a single argument of {@code exType},
5352      * and immediately throw it as an exception.
5353      * The method type will nominally specify a return of {@code returnType}.
5354      * The return type may be anything convenient:  It doesn't matter to the
5355      * method handle's behavior, since it will never return normally.
5356      * @param returnType the return type of the desired method handle
5357      * @param exType the parameter type of the desired method handle
5358      * @return method handle which can throw the given exceptions
5359      * @throws NullPointerException if either argument is null
5360      */
5361     public static MethodHandle throwException(Class<?> returnType, Class<? extends Throwable> exType) {
5362         if (!Throwable.class.isAssignableFrom(exType))
5363             throw new ClassCastException(exType.getName());
5364         return MethodHandleImpl.throwException(methodType(returnType, exType));
5365     }
5366 
5367     /**
5368      * Constructs a method handle representing a loop with several loop variables that are updated and checked upon each
5369      * iteration. Upon termination of the loop due to one of the predicates, a corresponding finalizer is run and
5370      * delivers the loop's result, which is the return value of the resulting handle.
5371      * <p>
5372      * Intuitively, every loop is formed by one or more "clauses", each specifying a local <em>iteration variable</em> and/or a loop
5373      * exit. Each iteration of the loop executes each clause in order. A clause can optionally update its iteration
5374      * variable; it can also optionally perform a test and conditional loop exit. In order to express this logic in
5375      * terms of method handles, each clause will specify up to four independent actions:<ul>
5376      * <li><em>init:</em> Before the loop executes, the initialization of an iteration variable {@code v} of type {@code V}.
5377      * <li><em>step:</em> When a clause executes, an update step for the iteration variable {@code v}.
5378      * <li><em>pred:</em> When a clause executes, a predicate execution to test for loop exit.
5379      * <li><em>fini:</em> If a clause causes a loop exit, a finalizer execution to compute the loop's return value.
5380      * </ul>
5381      * The full sequence of all iteration variable types, in clause order, will be notated as {@code (V...)}.
5382      * The values themselves will be {@code (v...)}.  When we speak of "parameter lists", we will usually
5383      * be referring to types, but in some contexts (describing execution) the lists will be of actual values.
5384      * <p>
5385      * Some of these clause parts may be omitted according to certain rules, and useful default behavior is provided in
5386      * this case. See below for a detailed description.
5387      * <p>
5388      * <em>Parameters optional everywhere:</em>
5389      * Each clause function is allowed but not required to accept a parameter for each iteration variable {@code v}.
5390      * As an exception, the init functions cannot take any {@code v} parameters,
5391      * because those values are not yet computed when the init functions are executed.
5392      * Any clause function may neglect to take any trailing subsequence of parameters it is entitled to take.
5393      * In fact, any clause function may take no arguments at all.
5394      * <p>
5395      * <em>Loop parameters:</em>
5396      * A clause function may take all the iteration variable values it is entitled to, in which case
5397      * it may also take more trailing parameters. Such extra values are called <em>loop parameters</em>,
5398      * with their types and values notated as {@code (A...)} and {@code (a...)}.
5399      * These become the parameters of the resulting loop handle, to be supplied whenever the loop is executed.
5400      * (Since init functions do not accept iteration variables {@code v}, any parameter to an
5401      * init function is automatically a loop parameter {@code a}.)
5402      * As with iteration variables, clause functions are allowed but not required to accept loop parameters.
5403      * These loop parameters act as loop-invariant values visible across the whole loop.
5404      * <p>
5405      * <em>Parameters visible everywhere:</em>
5406      * Each non-init clause function is permitted to observe the entire loop state, because it can be passed the full
5407      * list {@code (v... a...)} of current iteration variable values and incoming loop parameters.
5408      * The init functions can observe initial pre-loop state, in the form {@code (a...)}.
5409      * Most clause functions will not need all of this information, but they will be formally connected to it
5410      * as if by {@link #dropArguments}.
5411      * <a id="astar"></a>
5412      * More specifically, we shall use the notation {@code (V*)} to express an arbitrary prefix of a full
5413      * sequence {@code (V...)} (and likewise for {@code (v*)}, {@code (A*)}, {@code (a*)}).
5414      * In that notation, the general form of an init function parameter list
5415      * is {@code (A*)}, and the general form of a non-init function parameter list is {@code (V*)} or {@code (V... A*)}.
5416      * <p>
5417      * <em>Checking clause structure:</em>
5418      * Given a set of clauses, there is a number of checks and adjustments performed to connect all the parts of the
5419      * loop. They are spelled out in detail in the steps below. In these steps, every occurrence of the word "must"
5420      * corresponds to a place where {@link IllegalArgumentException} will be thrown if the required constraint is not
5421      * met by the inputs to the loop combinator.
5422      * <p>
5423      * <em>Effectively identical sequences:</em>
5424      * <a id="effid"></a>
5425      * A parameter list {@code A} is defined to be <em>effectively identical</em> to another parameter list {@code B}
5426      * if {@code A} and {@code B} are identical, or if {@code A} is shorter and is identical with a proper prefix of {@code B}.
5427      * When speaking of an unordered set of parameter lists, we say they the set is "effectively identical"
5428      * as a whole if the set contains a longest list, and all members of the set are effectively identical to
5429      * that longest list.
5430      * For example, any set of type sequences of the form {@code (V*)} is effectively identical,
5431      * and the same is true if more sequences of the form {@code (V... A*)} are added.
5432      * <p>
5433      * <em>Step 0: Determine clause structure.</em><ol type="a">
5434      * <li>The clause array (of type {@code MethodHandle[][]}) must be non-{@code null} and contain at least one element.
5435      * <li>The clause array may not contain {@code null}s or sub-arrays longer than four elements.
5436      * <li>Clauses shorter than four elements are treated as if they were padded by {@code null} elements to length
5437      * four. Padding takes place by appending elements to the array.
5438      * <li>Clauses with all {@code null}s are disregarded.
5439      * <li>Each clause is treated as a four-tuple of functions, called "init", "step", "pred", and "fini".
5440      * </ol>
5441      * <p>
5442      * <em>Step 1A: Determine iteration variable types {@code (V...)}.</em><ol type="a">
5443      * <li>The iteration variable type for each clause is determined using the clause's init and step return types.
5444      * <li>If both functions are omitted, there is no iteration variable for the corresponding clause ({@code void} is
5445      * used as the type to indicate that). If one of them is omitted, the other's return type defines the clause's
5446      * iteration variable type. If both are given, the common return type (they must be identical) defines the clause's
5447      * iteration variable type.
5448      * <li>Form the list of return types (in clause order), omitting all occurrences of {@code void}.
5449      * <li>This list of types is called the "iteration variable types" ({@code (V...)}).
5450      * </ol>
5451      * <p>
5452      * <em>Step 1B: Determine loop parameters {@code (A...)}.</em><ul>
5453      * <li>Examine and collect init function parameter lists (which are of the form {@code (A*)}).
5454      * <li>Examine and collect the suffixes of the step, pred, and fini parameter lists, after removing the iteration variable types.
5455      * (They must have the form {@code (V... A*)}; collect the {@code (A*)} parts only.)
5456      * <li>Do not collect suffixes from step, pred, and fini parameter lists that do not begin with all the iteration variable types.
5457      * (These types will be checked in step 2, along with all the clause function types.)
5458      * <li>Omitted clause functions are ignored.  (Equivalently, they are deemed to have empty parameter lists.)
5459      * <li>All of the collected parameter lists must be effectively identical.
5460      * <li>The longest parameter list (which is necessarily unique) is called the "external parameter list" ({@code (A...)}).
5461      * <li>If there is no such parameter list, the external parameter list is taken to be the empty sequence.
5462      * <li>The combined list consisting of iteration variable types followed by the external parameter types is called
5463      * the "internal parameter list".
5464      * </ul>
5465      * <p>
5466      * <em>Step 1C: Determine loop return type.</em><ol type="a">
5467      * <li>Examine fini function return types, disregarding omitted fini functions.
5468      * <li>If there are no fini functions, the loop return type is {@code void}.
5469      * <li>Otherwise, the common return type {@code R} of the fini functions (their return types must be identical) defines the loop return
5470      * type.
5471      * </ol>
5472      * <p>
5473      * <em>Step 1D: Check other types.</em><ol type="a">
5474      * <li>There must be at least one non-omitted pred function.
5475      * <li>Every non-omitted pred function must have a {@code boolean} return type.
5476      * </ol>
5477      * <p>
5478      * <em>Step 2: Determine parameter lists.</em><ol type="a">
5479      * <li>The parameter list for the resulting loop handle will be the external parameter list {@code (A...)}.
5480      * <li>The parameter list for init functions will be adjusted to the external parameter list.
5481      * (Note that their parameter lists are already effectively identical to this list.)
5482      * <li>The parameter list for every non-omitted, non-init (step, pred, and fini) function must be
5483      * effectively identical to the internal parameter list {@code (V... A...)}.
5484      * </ol>
5485      * <p>
5486      * <em>Step 3: Fill in omitted functions.</em><ol type="a">
5487      * <li>If an init function is omitted, use a {@linkplain #empty default value} for the clause's iteration variable
5488      * type.
5489      * <li>If a step function is omitted, use an {@linkplain #identity identity function} of the clause's iteration
5490      * variable type; insert dropped argument parameters before the identity function parameter for the non-{@code void}
5491      * iteration variables of preceding clauses. (This will turn the loop variable into a local loop invariant.)
5492      * <li>If a pred function is omitted, use a constant {@code true} function. (This will keep the loop going, as far
5493      * as this clause is concerned.  Note that in such cases the corresponding fini function is unreachable.)
5494      * <li>If a fini function is omitted, use a {@linkplain #empty default value} for the
5495      * loop return type.
5496      * </ol>
5497      * <p>
5498      * <em>Step 4: Fill in missing parameter types.</em><ol type="a">
5499      * <li>At this point, every init function parameter list is effectively identical to the external parameter list {@code (A...)},
5500      * but some lists may be shorter. For every init function with a short parameter list, pad out the end of the list.
5501      * <li>At this point, every non-init function parameter list is effectively identical to the internal parameter
5502      * list {@code (V... A...)}, but some lists may be shorter. For every non-init function with a short parameter list,
5503      * pad out the end of the list.
5504      * <li>Argument lists are padded out by {@linkplain #dropArgumentsToMatch(MethodHandle, int, List, int) dropping unused trailing arguments}.
5505      * </ol>
5506      * <p>
5507      * <em>Final observations.</em><ol type="a">
5508      * <li>After these steps, all clauses have been adjusted by supplying omitted functions and arguments.
5509      * <li>All init functions have a common parameter type list {@code (A...)}, which the final loop handle will also have.
5510      * <li>All fini functions have a common return type {@code R}, which the final loop handle will also have.
5511      * <li>All non-init functions have a common parameter type list {@code (V... A...)}, of
5512      * (non-{@code void}) iteration variables {@code V} followed by loop parameters.
5513      * <li>Each pair of init and step functions agrees in their return type {@code V}.
5514      * <li>Each non-init function will be able to observe the current values {@code (v...)} of all iteration variables.
5515      * <li>Every function will be able to observe the incoming values {@code (a...)} of all loop parameters.
5516      * </ol>
5517      * <p>
5518      * <em>Example.</em> As a consequence of step 1A above, the {@code loop} combinator has the following property:
5519      * <ul>
5520      * <li>Given {@code N} clauses {@code Cn = {null, Sn, Pn}} with {@code n = 1..N}.
5521      * <li>Suppose predicate handles {@code Pn} are either {@code null} or have no parameters.
5522      * (Only one {@code Pn} has to be non-{@code null}.)
5523      * <li>Suppose step handles {@code Sn} have signatures {@code (B1..BX)Rn}, for some constant {@code X>=N}.
5524      * <li>Suppose {@code Q} is the count of non-void types {@code Rn}, and {@code (V1...VQ)} is the sequence of those types.
5525      * <li>It must be that {@code Vn == Bn} for {@code n = 1..min(X,Q)}.
5526      * <li>The parameter types {@code Vn} will be interpreted as loop-local state elements {@code (V...)}.
5527      * <li>Any remaining types {@code BQ+1..BX} (if {@code Q<X}) will determine
5528      * the resulting loop handle's parameter types {@code (A...)}.
5529      * </ul>
5530      * In this example, the loop handle parameters {@code (A...)} were derived from the step functions,
5531      * which is natural if most of the loop computation happens in the steps.  For some loops,
5532      * the burden of computation might be heaviest in the pred functions, and so the pred functions
5533      * might need to accept the loop parameter values.  For loops with complex exit logic, the fini
5534      * functions might need to accept loop parameters, and likewise for loops with complex entry logic,
5535      * where the init functions will need the extra parameters.  For such reasons, the rules for
5536      * determining these parameters are as symmetric as possible, across all clause parts.
5537      * In general, the loop parameters function as common invariant values across the whole
5538      * loop, while the iteration variables function as common variant values, or (if there is
5539      * no step function) as internal loop invariant temporaries.
5540      * <p>
5541      * <em>Loop execution.</em><ol type="a">
5542      * <li>When the loop is called, the loop input values are saved in locals, to be passed to
5543      * every clause function. These locals are loop invariant.
5544      * <li>Each init function is executed in clause order (passing the external arguments {@code (a...)})
5545      * and the non-{@code void} values are saved (as the iteration variables {@code (v...)}) into locals.
5546      * These locals will be loop varying (unless their steps behave as identity functions, as noted above).
5547      * <li>All function executions (except init functions) will be passed the internal parameter list, consisting of
5548      * the non-{@code void} iteration values {@code (v...)} (in clause order) and then the loop inputs {@code (a...)}
5549      * (in argument order).
5550      * <li>The step and pred functions are then executed, in clause order (step before pred), until a pred function
5551      * returns {@code false}.
5552      * <li>The non-{@code void} result from a step function call is used to update the corresponding value in the
5553      * sequence {@code (v...)} of loop variables.
5554      * The updated value is immediately visible to all subsequent function calls.
5555      * <li>If a pred function returns {@code false}, the corresponding fini function is called, and the resulting value
5556      * (of type {@code R}) is returned from the loop as a whole.
5557      * <li>If all the pred functions always return true, no fini function is ever invoked, and the loop cannot exit
5558      * except by throwing an exception.
5559      * </ol>
5560      * <p>
5561      * <em>Usage tips.</em>
5562      * <ul>
5563      * <li>Although each step function will receive the current values of <em>all</em> the loop variables,
5564      * sometimes a step function only needs to observe the current value of its own variable.
5565      * In that case, the step function may need to explicitly {@linkplain #dropArguments drop all preceding loop variables}.
5566      * This will require mentioning their types, in an expression like {@code dropArguments(step, 0, V0.class, ...)}.
5567      * <li>Loop variables are not required to vary; they can be loop invariant.  A clause can create
5568      * a loop invariant by a suitable init function with no step, pred, or fini function.  This may be
5569      * useful to "wire" an incoming loop argument into the step or pred function of an adjacent loop variable.
5570      * <li>If some of the clause functions are virtual methods on an instance, the instance
5571      * itself can be conveniently placed in an initial invariant loop "variable", using an initial clause
5572      * like {@code new MethodHandle[]{identity(ObjType.class)}}.  In that case, the instance reference
5573      * will be the first iteration variable value, and it will be easy to use virtual
5574      * methods as clause parts, since all of them will take a leading instance reference matching that value.
5575      * </ul>
5576      * <p>
5577      * Here is pseudocode for the resulting loop handle. As above, {@code V} and {@code v} represent the types
5578      * and values of loop variables; {@code A} and {@code a} represent arguments passed to the whole loop;
5579      * and {@code R} is the common result type of all finalizers as well as of the resulting loop.
5580      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
5581      * V... init...(A...);
5582      * boolean pred...(V..., A...);
5583      * V... step...(V..., A...);
5584      * R fini...(V..., A...);
5585      * R loop(A... a) {
5586      *   V... v... = init...(a...);
5587      *   for (;;) {
5588      *     for ((v, p, s, f) in (v..., pred..., step..., fini...)) {
5589      *       v = s(v..., a...);
5590      *       if (!p(v..., a...)) {
5591      *         return f(v..., a...);
5592      *       }
5593      *     }
5594      *   }
5595      * }
5596      * }</pre></blockquote>
5597      * Note that the parameter type lists {@code (V...)} and {@code (A...)} have been expanded
5598      * to their full length, even though individual clause functions may neglect to take them all.
5599      * As noted above, missing parameters are filled in as if by {@link #dropArgumentsToMatch(MethodHandle, int, List, int)}.
5600      *
5601      * @apiNote Example:
5602      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
5603      * // iterative implementation of the factorial function as a loop handle
5604      * static int one(int k) { return 1; }
5605      * static int inc(int i, int acc, int k) { return i + 1; }
5606      * static int mult(int i, int acc, int k) { return i * acc; }
5607      * static boolean pred(int i, int acc, int k) { return i < k; }
5608      * static int fin(int i, int acc, int k) { return acc; }
5609      * // assume MH_one, MH_inc, MH_mult, MH_pred, and MH_fin are handles to the above methods
5610      * // null initializer for counter, should initialize to 0
5611      * MethodHandle[] counterClause = new MethodHandle[]{null, MH_inc};
5612      * MethodHandle[] accumulatorClause = new MethodHandle[]{MH_one, MH_mult, MH_pred, MH_fin};
5613      * MethodHandle loop = MethodHandles.loop(counterClause, accumulatorClause);
5614      * assertEquals(120, loop.invoke(5));
5615      * }</pre></blockquote>
5616      * The same example, dropping arguments and using combinators:
5617      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
5618      * // simplified implementation of the factorial function as a loop handle
5619      * static int inc(int i) { return i + 1; } // drop acc, k
5620      * static int mult(int i, int acc) { return i * acc; } //drop k
5621      * static boolean cmp(int i, int k) { return i < k; }
5622      * // assume MH_inc, MH_mult, and MH_cmp are handles to the above methods
5623      * // null initializer for counter, should initialize to 0
5624      * MethodHandle MH_one = MethodHandles.constant(int.class, 1);
5625      * MethodHandle MH_pred = MethodHandles.dropArguments(MH_cmp, 1, int.class); // drop acc
5626      * MethodHandle MH_fin = MethodHandles.dropArguments(MethodHandles.identity(int.class), 0, int.class); // drop i
5627      * MethodHandle[] counterClause = new MethodHandle[]{null, MH_inc};
5628      * MethodHandle[] accumulatorClause = new MethodHandle[]{MH_one, MH_mult, MH_pred, MH_fin};
5629      * MethodHandle loop = MethodHandles.loop(counterClause, accumulatorClause);
5630      * assertEquals(720, loop.invoke(6));
5631      * }</pre></blockquote>
5632      * A similar example, using a helper object to hold a loop parameter:
5633      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
5634      * // instance-based implementation of the factorial function as a loop handle
5635      * static class FacLoop {
5636      *   final int k;
5637      *   FacLoop(int k) { this.k = k; }
5638      *   int inc(int i) { return i + 1; }
5639      *   int mult(int i, int acc) { return i * acc; }
5640      *   boolean pred(int i) { return i < k; }
5641      *   int fin(int i, int acc) { return acc; }
5642      * }
5643      * // assume MH_FacLoop is a handle to the constructor
5644      * // assume MH_inc, MH_mult, MH_pred, and MH_fin are handles to the above methods
5645      * // null initializer for counter, should initialize to 0
5646      * MethodHandle MH_one = MethodHandles.constant(int.class, 1);
5647      * MethodHandle[] instanceClause = new MethodHandle[]{MH_FacLoop};
5648      * MethodHandle[] counterClause = new MethodHandle[]{null, MH_inc};
5649      * MethodHandle[] accumulatorClause = new MethodHandle[]{MH_one, MH_mult, MH_pred, MH_fin};
5650      * MethodHandle loop = MethodHandles.loop(instanceClause, counterClause, accumulatorClause);
5651      * assertEquals(5040, loop.invoke(7));
5652      * }</pre></blockquote>
5653      *
5654      * @param clauses an array of arrays (4-tuples) of {@link MethodHandle}s adhering to the rules described above.
5655      *
5656      * @return a method handle embodying the looping behavior as defined by the arguments.
5657      *
5658      * @throws IllegalArgumentException in case any of the constraints described above is violated.
5659      *
5660      * @see MethodHandles#whileLoop(MethodHandle, MethodHandle, MethodHandle)
5661      * @see MethodHandles#doWhileLoop(MethodHandle, MethodHandle, MethodHandle)
5662      * @see MethodHandles#countedLoop(MethodHandle, MethodHandle, MethodHandle)
5663      * @see MethodHandles#iteratedLoop(MethodHandle, MethodHandle, MethodHandle)
5664      * @since 9
5665      */
5666     public static MethodHandle loop(MethodHandle[]... clauses) {
5667         // Step 0: determine clause structure.
5668         loopChecks0(clauses);
5669 
5670         List<MethodHandle> init = new ArrayList<>();
5671         List<MethodHandle> step = new ArrayList<>();
5672         List<MethodHandle> pred = new ArrayList<>();
5673         List<MethodHandle> fini = new ArrayList<>();
5674 
5675         Stream.of(clauses).filter(c -> Stream.of(c).anyMatch(Objects::nonNull)).forEach(clause -> {
5676             init.add(clause[0]); // all clauses have at least length 1
5677             step.add(clause.length <= 1 ? null : clause[1]);
5678             pred.add(clause.length <= 2 ? null : clause[2]);
5679             fini.add(clause.length <= 3 ? null : clause[3]);
5680         });
5681 
5682         assert Stream.of(init, step, pred, fini).map(List::size).distinct().count() == 1;
5683         final int nclauses = init.size();
5684 
5685         // Step 1A: determine iteration variables (V...).
5686         final List<Class<?>> iterationVariableTypes = new ArrayList<>();
5687         for (int i = 0; i < nclauses; ++i) {
5688             MethodHandle in = init.get(i);
5689             MethodHandle st = step.get(i);
5690             if (in == null && st == null) {
5691                 iterationVariableTypes.add(void.class);
5692             } else if (in != null && st != null) {
5693                 loopChecks1a(i, in, st);
5694                 iterationVariableTypes.add(in.type().returnType());
5695             } else {
5696                 iterationVariableTypes.add(in == null ? st.type().returnType() : in.type().returnType());
5697             }
5698         }
5699         final List<Class<?>> commonPrefix = iterationVariableTypes.stream().filter(t -> t != void.class).
5700                 collect(Collectors.toList());
5701 
5702         // Step 1B: determine loop parameters (A...).
5703         final List<Class<?>> commonSuffix = buildCommonSuffix(init, step, pred, fini, commonPrefix.size());
5704         loopChecks1b(init, commonSuffix);
5705 
5706         // Step 1C: determine loop return type.
5707         // Step 1D: check other types.
5708         // local variable required here; see JDK-8223553
5709         Stream<Class<?>> cstream = fini.stream().filter(Objects::nonNull).map(MethodHandle::type)
5710                 .map(MethodType::returnType);
5711         final Class<?> loopReturnType = cstream.findFirst().orElse(void.class);
5712         loopChecks1cd(pred, fini, loopReturnType);
5713 
5714         // Step 2: determine parameter lists.
5715         final List<Class<?>> commonParameterSequence = new ArrayList<>(commonPrefix);
5716         commonParameterSequence.addAll(commonSuffix);
5717         loopChecks2(step, pred, fini, commonParameterSequence);
5718 
5719         // Step 3: fill in omitted functions.
5720         for (int i = 0; i < nclauses; ++i) {
5721             Class<?> t = iterationVariableTypes.get(i);
5722             if (init.get(i) == null) {
5723                 init.set(i, empty(methodType(t, commonSuffix)));
5724             }
5725             if (step.get(i) == null) {
5726                 step.set(i, dropArgumentsToMatch(identityOrVoid(t), 0, commonParameterSequence, i));
5727             }
5728             if (pred.get(i) == null) {
5729                 pred.set(i, dropArguments0(constant(boolean.class, true), 0, commonParameterSequence));
5730             }
5731             if (fini.get(i) == null) {
5732                 fini.set(i, empty(methodType(t, commonParameterSequence)));
5733             }
5734         }
5735 
5736         // Step 4: fill in missing parameter types.
5737         // Also convert all handles to fixed-arity handles.
5738         List<MethodHandle> finit = fixArities(fillParameterTypes(init, commonSuffix));
5739         List<MethodHandle> fstep = fixArities(fillParameterTypes(step, commonParameterSequence));
5740         List<MethodHandle> fpred = fixArities(fillParameterTypes(pred, commonParameterSequence));
5741         List<MethodHandle> ffini = fixArities(fillParameterTypes(fini, commonParameterSequence));
5742 
5743         assert finit.stream().map(MethodHandle::type).map(MethodType::parameterList).
5744                 allMatch(pl -> pl.equals(commonSuffix));
5745         assert Stream.of(fstep, fpred, ffini).flatMap(List::stream).map(MethodHandle::type).map(MethodType::parameterList).
5746                 allMatch(pl -> pl.equals(commonParameterSequence));
5747 
5748         return MethodHandleImpl.makeLoop(loopReturnType, commonSuffix, finit, fstep, fpred, ffini);
5749     }
5750 
5751     private static void loopChecks0(MethodHandle[][] clauses) {
5752         if (clauses == null || clauses.length == 0) {
5753             throw newIllegalArgumentException("null or no clauses passed");
5754         }
5755         if (Stream.of(clauses).anyMatch(Objects::isNull)) {
5756             throw newIllegalArgumentException("null clauses are not allowed");
5757         }
5758         if (Stream.of(clauses).anyMatch(c -> c.length > 4)) {
5759             throw newIllegalArgumentException("All loop clauses must be represented as MethodHandle arrays with at most 4 elements.");
5760         }
5761     }
5762 
5763     private static void loopChecks1a(int i, MethodHandle in, MethodHandle st) {
5764         if (in.type().returnType() != st.type().returnType()) {
5765             throw misMatchedTypes("clause " + i + ": init and step return types", in.type().returnType(),
5766                     st.type().returnType());
5767         }
5768     }
5769 
5770     private static List<Class<?>> longestParameterList(Stream<MethodHandle> mhs, int skipSize) {
5771         final List<Class<?>> empty = List.of();
5772         final List<Class<?>> longest = mhs.filter(Objects::nonNull).
5773                 // take only those that can contribute to a common suffix because they are longer than the prefix
5774                         map(MethodHandle::type).
5775                         filter(t -> t.parameterCount() > skipSize).
5776                         map(MethodType::parameterList).
5777                         reduce((p, q) -> p.size() >= q.size() ? p : q).orElse(empty);
5778         return longest.size() == 0 ? empty : longest.subList(skipSize, longest.size());
5779     }
5780 
5781     private static List<Class<?>> longestParameterList(List<List<Class<?>>> lists) {
5782         final List<Class<?>> empty = List.of();
5783         return lists.stream().reduce((p, q) -> p.size() >= q.size() ? p : q).orElse(empty);
5784     }
5785 
5786     private static List<Class<?>> buildCommonSuffix(List<MethodHandle> init, List<MethodHandle> step, List<MethodHandle> pred, List<MethodHandle> fini, int cpSize) {
5787         final List<Class<?>> longest1 = longestParameterList(Stream.of(step, pred, fini).flatMap(List::stream), cpSize);
5788         final List<Class<?>> longest2 = longestParameterList(init.stream(), 0);
5789         return longestParameterList(Arrays.asList(longest1, longest2));
5790     }
5791 
5792     private static void loopChecks1b(List<MethodHandle> init, List<Class<?>> commonSuffix) {
5793         if (init.stream().filter(Objects::nonNull).map(MethodHandle::type).
5794                 anyMatch(t -> !t.effectivelyIdenticalParameters(0, commonSuffix))) {
5795             throw newIllegalArgumentException("found non-effectively identical init parameter type lists: " + init +
5796                     " (common suffix: " + commonSuffix + ")");
5797         }
5798     }
5799 
5800     private static void loopChecks1cd(List<MethodHandle> pred, List<MethodHandle> fini, Class<?> loopReturnType) {
5801         if (fini.stream().filter(Objects::nonNull).map(MethodHandle::type).map(MethodType::returnType).
5802                 anyMatch(t -> t != loopReturnType)) {
5803             throw newIllegalArgumentException("found non-identical finalizer return types: " + fini + " (return type: " +
5804                     loopReturnType + ")");
5805         }
5806 
5807         if (!pred.stream().filter(Objects::nonNull).findFirst().isPresent()) {
5808             throw newIllegalArgumentException("no predicate found", pred);
5809         }
5810         if (pred.stream().filter(Objects::nonNull).map(MethodHandle::type).map(MethodType::returnType).
5811                 anyMatch(t -> t != boolean.class)) {
5812             throw newIllegalArgumentException("predicates must have boolean return type", pred);
5813         }
5814     }
5815 
5816     private static void loopChecks2(List<MethodHandle> step, List<MethodHandle> pred, List<MethodHandle> fini, List<Class<?>> commonParameterSequence) {
5817         if (Stream.of(step, pred, fini).flatMap(List::stream).filter(Objects::nonNull).map(MethodHandle::type).
5818                 anyMatch(t -> !t.effectivelyIdenticalParameters(0, commonParameterSequence))) {
5819             throw newIllegalArgumentException("found non-effectively identical parameter type lists:\nstep: " + step +
5820                     "\npred: " + pred + "\nfini: " + fini + " (common parameter sequence: " + commonParameterSequence + ")");
5821         }
5822     }
5823 
5824     private static List<MethodHandle> fillParameterTypes(List<MethodHandle> hs, final List<Class<?>> targetParams) {
5825         return hs.stream().map(h -> {
5826             int pc = h.type().parameterCount();
5827             int tpsize = targetParams.size();
5828             return pc < tpsize ? dropArguments0(h, pc, targetParams.subList(pc, tpsize)) : h;
5829         }).collect(Collectors.toList());
5830     }
5831 
5832     private static List<MethodHandle> fixArities(List<MethodHandle> hs) {
5833         return hs.stream().map(MethodHandle::asFixedArity).collect(Collectors.toList());
5834     }
5835 
5836     /**
5837      * Constructs a {@code while} loop from an initializer, a body, and a predicate.
5838      * This is a convenience wrapper for the {@linkplain #loop(MethodHandle[][]) generic loop combinator}.
5839      * <p>
5840      * The {@code pred} handle describes the loop condition; and {@code body}, its body. The loop resulting from this
5841      * method will, in each iteration, first evaluate the predicate and then execute its body (if the predicate
5842      * evaluates to {@code true}).
5843      * The loop will terminate once the predicate evaluates to {@code false} (the body will not be executed in this case).
5844      * <p>
5845      * The {@code init} handle describes the initial value of an additional optional loop-local variable.
5846      * In each iteration, this loop-local variable, if present, will be passed to the {@code body}
5847      * and updated with the value returned from its invocation. The result of loop execution will be
5848      * the final value of the additional loop-local variable (if present).
5849      * <p>
5850      * The following rules hold for these argument handles:<ul>
5851      * <li>The {@code body} handle must not be {@code null}; its type must be of the form
5852      * {@code (V A...)V}, where {@code V} is non-{@code void}, or else {@code (A...)void}.
5853      * (In the {@code void} case, we assign the type {@code void} to the name {@code V},
5854      * and we will write {@code (V A...)V} with the understanding that a {@code void} type {@code V}
5855      * is quietly dropped from the parameter list, leaving {@code (A...)V}.)
5856      * <li>The parameter list {@code (V A...)} of the body is called the <em>internal parameter list</em>.
5857      * It will constrain the parameter lists of the other loop parts.
5858      * <li>If the iteration variable type {@code V} is dropped from the internal parameter list, the resulting shorter
5859      * list {@code (A...)} is called the <em>external parameter list</em>.
5860      * <li>The body return type {@code V}, if non-{@code void}, determines the type of an
5861      * additional state variable of the loop.
5862      * The body must both accept and return a value of this type {@code V}.
5863      * <li>If {@code init} is non-{@code null}, it must have return type {@code V}.
5864      * Its parameter list (of some <a href="MethodHandles.html#astar">form {@code (A*)}</a>) must be
5865      * <a href="MethodHandles.html#effid">effectively identical</a>
5866      * to the external parameter list {@code (A...)}.
5867      * <li>If {@code init} is {@code null}, the loop variable will be initialized to its
5868      * {@linkplain #empty default value}.
5869      * <li>The {@code pred} handle must not be {@code null}.  It must have {@code boolean} as its return type.
5870      * Its parameter list (either empty or of the form {@code (V A*)}) must be
5871      * effectively identical to the internal parameter list.
5872      * </ul>
5873      * <p>
5874      * The resulting loop handle's result type and parameter signature are determined as follows:<ul>
5875      * <li>The loop handle's result type is the result type {@code V} of the body.
5876      * <li>The loop handle's parameter types are the types {@code (A...)},
5877      * from the external parameter list.
5878      * </ul>
5879      * <p>
5880      * Here is pseudocode for the resulting loop handle. In the code, {@code V}/{@code v} represent the type / value of
5881      * the sole loop variable as well as the result type of the loop; and {@code A}/{@code a}, that of the argument
5882      * passed to the loop.
5883      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
5884      * V init(A...);
5885      * boolean pred(V, A...);
5886      * V body(V, A...);
5887      * V whileLoop(A... a...) {
5888      *   V v = init(a...);
5889      *   while (pred(v, a...)) {
5890      *     v = body(v, a...);
5891      *   }
5892      *   return v;
5893      * }
5894      * }</pre></blockquote>
5895      *
5896      * @apiNote Example:
5897      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
5898      * // implement the zip function for lists as a loop handle
5899      * static List<String> initZip(Iterator<String> a, Iterator<String> b) { return new ArrayList<>(); }
5900      * static boolean zipPred(List<String> zip, Iterator<String> a, Iterator<String> b) { return a.hasNext() && b.hasNext(); }
5901      * static List<String> zipStep(List<String> zip, Iterator<String> a, Iterator<String> b) {
5902      *   zip.add(a.next());
5903      *   zip.add(b.next());
5904      *   return zip;
5905      * }
5906      * // assume MH_initZip, MH_zipPred, and MH_zipStep are handles to the above methods
5907      * MethodHandle loop = MethodHandles.whileLoop(MH_initZip, MH_zipPred, MH_zipStep);
5908      * List<String> a = Arrays.asList("a", "b", "c", "d");
5909      * List<String> b = Arrays.asList("e", "f", "g", "h");
5910      * List<String> zipped = Arrays.asList("a", "e", "b", "f", "c", "g", "d", "h");
5911      * assertEquals(zipped, (List<String>) loop.invoke(a.iterator(), b.iterator()));
5912      * }</pre></blockquote>
5913      *
5914      *
5915      * @apiNote The implementation of this method can be expressed as follows:
5916      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
5917      * MethodHandle whileLoop(MethodHandle init, MethodHandle pred, MethodHandle body) {
5918      *     MethodHandle fini = (body.type().returnType() == void.class
5919      *                         ? null : identity(body.type().returnType()));
5920      *     MethodHandle[]
5921      *         checkExit = { null, null, pred, fini },
5922      *         varBody   = { init, body };
5923      *     return loop(checkExit, varBody);
5924      * }
5925      * }</pre></blockquote>
5926      *
5927      * @param init optional initializer, providing the initial value of the loop variable.
5928      *             May be {@code null}, implying a default initial value.  See above for other constraints.
5929      * @param pred condition for the loop, which may not be {@code null}. Its result type must be {@code boolean}. See
5930      *             above for other constraints.
5931      * @param body body of the loop, which may not be {@code null}. It controls the loop parameters and result type.
5932      *             See above for other constraints.
5933      *
5934      * @return a method handle implementing the {@code while} loop as described by the arguments.
5935      * @throws IllegalArgumentException if the rules for the arguments are violated.
5936      * @throws NullPointerException if {@code pred} or {@code body} are {@code null}.
5937      *
5938      * @see #loop(MethodHandle[][])
5939      * @see #doWhileLoop(MethodHandle, MethodHandle, MethodHandle)
5940      * @since 9
5941      */
5942     public static MethodHandle whileLoop(MethodHandle init, MethodHandle pred, MethodHandle body) {
5943         whileLoopChecks(init, pred, body);
5944         MethodHandle fini = identityOrVoid(body.type().returnType());
5945         MethodHandle[] checkExit = { null, null, pred, fini };
5946         MethodHandle[] varBody = { init, body };
5947         return loop(checkExit, varBody);
5948     }
5949 
5950     /**
5951      * Constructs a {@code do-while} loop from an initializer, a body, and a predicate.
5952      * This is a convenience wrapper for the {@linkplain #loop(MethodHandle[][]) generic loop combinator}.
5953      * <p>
5954      * The {@code pred} handle describes the loop condition; and {@code body}, its body. The loop resulting from this
5955      * method will, in each iteration, first execute its body and then evaluate the predicate.
5956      * The loop will terminate once the predicate evaluates to {@code false} after an execution of the body.
5957      * <p>
5958      * The {@code init} handle describes the initial value of an additional optional loop-local variable.
5959      * In each iteration, this loop-local variable, if present, will be passed to the {@code body}
5960      * and updated with the value returned from its invocation. The result of loop execution will be
5961      * the final value of the additional loop-local variable (if present).
5962      * <p>
5963      * The following rules hold for these argument handles:<ul>
5964      * <li>The {@code body} handle must not be {@code null}; its type must be of the form
5965      * {@code (V A...)V}, where {@code V} is non-{@code void}, or else {@code (A...)void}.
5966      * (In the {@code void} case, we assign the type {@code void} to the name {@code V},
5967      * and we will write {@code (V A...)V} with the understanding that a {@code void} type {@code V}
5968      * is quietly dropped from the parameter list, leaving {@code (A...)V}.)
5969      * <li>The parameter list {@code (V A...)} of the body is called the <em>internal parameter list</em>.
5970      * It will constrain the parameter lists of the other loop parts.
5971      * <li>If the iteration variable type {@code V} is dropped from the internal parameter list, the resulting shorter
5972      * list {@code (A...)} is called the <em>external parameter list</em>.
5973      * <li>The body return type {@code V}, if non-{@code void}, determines the type of an
5974      * additional state variable of the loop.
5975      * The body must both accept and return a value of this type {@code V}.
5976      * <li>If {@code init} is non-{@code null}, it must have return type {@code V}.
5977      * Its parameter list (of some <a href="MethodHandles.html#astar">form {@code (A*)}</a>) must be
5978      * <a href="MethodHandles.html#effid">effectively identical</a>
5979      * to the external parameter list {@code (A...)}.
5980      * <li>If {@code init} is {@code null}, the loop variable will be initialized to its
5981      * {@linkplain #empty default value}.
5982      * <li>The {@code pred} handle must not be {@code null}.  It must have {@code boolean} as its return type.
5983      * Its parameter list (either empty or of the form {@code (V A*)}) must be
5984      * effectively identical to the internal parameter list.
5985      * </ul>
5986      * <p>
5987      * The resulting loop handle's result type and parameter signature are determined as follows:<ul>
5988      * <li>The loop handle's result type is the result type {@code V} of the body.
5989      * <li>The loop handle's parameter types are the types {@code (A...)},
5990      * from the external parameter list.
5991      * </ul>
5992      * <p>
5993      * Here is pseudocode for the resulting loop handle. In the code, {@code V}/{@code v} represent the type / value of
5994      * the sole loop variable as well as the result type of the loop; and {@code A}/{@code a}, that of the argument
5995      * passed to the loop.
5996      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
5997      * V init(A...);
5998      * boolean pred(V, A...);
5999      * V body(V, A...);
6000      * V doWhileLoop(A... a...) {
6001      *   V v = init(a...);
6002      *   do {
6003      *     v = body(v, a...);
6004      *   } while (pred(v, a...));
6005      *   return v;
6006      * }
6007      * }</pre></blockquote>
6008      *
6009      * @apiNote Example:
6010      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
6011      * // int i = 0; while (i < limit) { ++i; } return i; => limit
6012      * static int zero(int limit) { return 0; }
6013      * static int step(int i, int limit) { return i + 1; }
6014      * static boolean pred(int i, int limit) { return i < limit; }
6015      * // assume MH_zero, MH_step, and MH_pred are handles to the above methods
6016      * MethodHandle loop = MethodHandles.doWhileLoop(MH_zero, MH_step, MH_pred);
6017      * assertEquals(23, loop.invoke(23));
6018      * }</pre></blockquote>
6019      *
6020      *
6021      * @apiNote The implementation of this method can be expressed as follows:
6022      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
6023      * MethodHandle doWhileLoop(MethodHandle init, MethodHandle body, MethodHandle pred) {
6024      *     MethodHandle fini = (body.type().returnType() == void.class
6025      *                         ? null : identity(body.type().returnType()));
6026      *     MethodHandle[] clause = { init, body, pred, fini };
6027      *     return loop(clause);
6028      * }
6029      * }</pre></blockquote>
6030      *
6031      * @param init optional initializer, providing the initial value of the loop variable.
6032      *             May be {@code null}, implying a default initial value.  See above for other constraints.
6033      * @param body body of the loop, which may not be {@code null}. It controls the loop parameters and result type.
6034      *             See above for other constraints.
6035      * @param pred condition for the loop, which may not be {@code null}. Its result type must be {@code boolean}. See
6036      *             above for other constraints.
6037      *
6038      * @return a method handle implementing the {@code while} loop as described by the arguments.
6039      * @throws IllegalArgumentException if the rules for the arguments are violated.
6040      * @throws NullPointerException if {@code pred} or {@code body} are {@code null}.
6041      *
6042      * @see #loop(MethodHandle[][])
6043      * @see #whileLoop(MethodHandle, MethodHandle, MethodHandle)
6044      * @since 9
6045      */
6046     public static MethodHandle doWhileLoop(MethodHandle init, MethodHandle body, MethodHandle pred) {
6047         whileLoopChecks(init, pred, body);
6048         MethodHandle fini = identityOrVoid(body.type().returnType());
6049         MethodHandle[] clause = {init, body, pred, fini };
6050         return loop(clause);
6051     }
6052 
6053     private static void whileLoopChecks(MethodHandle init, MethodHandle pred, MethodHandle body) {
6054         Objects.requireNonNull(pred);
6055         Objects.requireNonNull(body);
6056         MethodType bodyType = body.type();
6057         Class<?> returnType = bodyType.returnType();
6058         List<Class<?>> innerList = bodyType.parameterList();
6059         List<Class<?>> outerList = innerList;
6060         if (returnType == void.class) {
6061             // OK
6062         } else if (innerList.size() == 0 || innerList.get(0) != returnType) {
6063             // leading V argument missing => error
6064             MethodType expected = bodyType.insertParameterTypes(0, returnType);
6065             throw misMatchedTypes("body function", bodyType, expected);
6066         } else {
6067             outerList = innerList.subList(1, innerList.size());
6068         }
6069         MethodType predType = pred.type();
6070         if (predType.returnType() != boolean.class ||
6071                 !predType.effectivelyIdenticalParameters(0, innerList)) {
6072             throw misMatchedTypes("loop predicate", predType, methodType(boolean.class, innerList));
6073         }
6074         if (init != null) {
6075             MethodType initType = init.type();
6076             if (initType.returnType() != returnType ||
6077                     !initType.effectivelyIdenticalParameters(0, outerList)) {
6078                 throw misMatchedTypes("loop initializer", initType, methodType(returnType, outerList));
6079             }
6080         }
6081     }
6082 
6083     /**
6084      * Constructs a loop that runs a given number of iterations.
6085      * This is a convenience wrapper for the {@linkplain #loop(MethodHandle[][]) generic loop combinator}.
6086      * <p>
6087      * The number of iterations is determined by the {@code iterations} handle evaluation result.
6088      * The loop counter {@code i} is an extra loop iteration variable of type {@code int}.
6089      * It will be initialized to 0 and incremented by 1 in each iteration.
6090      * <p>
6091      * If the {@code body} handle returns a non-{@code void} type {@code V}, a leading loop iteration variable
6092      * of that type is also present.  This variable is initialized using the optional {@code init} handle,
6093      * or to the {@linkplain #empty default value} of type {@code V} if that handle is {@code null}.
6094      * <p>
6095      * In each iteration, the iteration variables are passed to an invocation of the {@code body} handle.
6096      * A non-{@code void} value returned from the body (of type {@code V}) updates the leading
6097      * iteration variable.
6098      * The result of the loop handle execution will be the final {@code V} value of that variable
6099      * (or {@code void} if there is no {@code V} variable).
6100      * <p>
6101      * The following rules hold for the argument handles:<ul>
6102      * <li>The {@code iterations} handle must not be {@code null}, and must return
6103      * the type {@code int}, referred to here as {@code I} in parameter type lists.
6104      * <li>The {@code body} handle must not be {@code null}; its type must be of the form
6105      * {@code (V I A...)V}, where {@code V} is non-{@code void}, or else {@code (I A...)void}.
6106      * (In the {@code void} case, we assign the type {@code void} to the name {@code V},
6107      * and we will write {@code (V I A...)V} with the understanding that a {@code void} type {@code V}
6108      * is quietly dropped from the parameter list, leaving {@code (I A...)V}.)
6109      * <li>The parameter list {@code (V I A...)} of the body contributes to a list
6110      * of types called the <em>internal parameter list</em>.
6111      * It will constrain the parameter lists of the other loop parts.
6112      * <li>As a special case, if the body contributes only {@code V} and {@code I} types,
6113      * with no additional {@code A} types, then the internal parameter list is extended by
6114      * the argument types {@code A...} of the {@code iterations} handle.
6115      * <li>If the iteration variable types {@code (V I)} are dropped from the internal parameter list, the resulting shorter
6116      * list {@code (A...)} is called the <em>external parameter list</em>.
6117      * <li>The body return type {@code V}, if non-{@code void}, determines the type of an
6118      * additional state variable of the loop.
6119      * The body must both accept a leading parameter and return a value of this type {@code V}.
6120      * <li>If {@code init} is non-{@code null}, it must have return type {@code V}.
6121      * Its parameter list (of some <a href="MethodHandles.html#astar">form {@code (A*)}</a>) must be
6122      * <a href="MethodHandles.html#effid">effectively identical</a>
6123      * to the external parameter list {@code (A...)}.
6124      * <li>If {@code init} is {@code null}, the loop variable will be initialized to its
6125      * {@linkplain #empty default value}.
6126      * <li>The parameter list of {@code iterations} (of some form {@code (A*)}) must be
6127      * effectively identical to the external parameter list {@code (A...)}.
6128      * </ul>
6129      * <p>
6130      * The resulting loop handle's result type and parameter signature are determined as follows:<ul>
6131      * <li>The loop handle's result type is the result type {@code V} of the body.
6132      * <li>The loop handle's parameter types are the types {@code (A...)},
6133      * from the external parameter list.
6134      * </ul>
6135      * <p>
6136      * Here is pseudocode for the resulting loop handle. In the code, {@code V}/{@code v} represent the type / value of
6137      * the second loop variable as well as the result type of the loop; and {@code A...}/{@code a...} represent
6138      * arguments passed to the loop.
6139      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
6140      * int iterations(A...);
6141      * V init(A...);
6142      * V body(V, int, A...);
6143      * V countedLoop(A... a...) {
6144      *   int end = iterations(a...);
6145      *   V v = init(a...);
6146      *   for (int i = 0; i < end; ++i) {
6147      *     v = body(v, i, a...);
6148      *   }
6149      *   return v;
6150      * }
6151      * }</pre></blockquote>
6152      *
6153      * @apiNote Example with a fully conformant body method:
6154      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
6155      * // String s = "Lambdaman!"; for (int i = 0; i < 13; ++i) { s = "na " + s; } return s;
6156      * // => a variation on a well known theme
6157      * static String step(String v, int counter, String init) { return "na " + v; }
6158      * // assume MH_step is a handle to the method above
6159      * MethodHandle fit13 = MethodHandles.constant(int.class, 13);
6160      * MethodHandle start = MethodHandles.identity(String.class);
6161      * MethodHandle loop = MethodHandles.countedLoop(fit13, start, MH_step);
6162      * assertEquals("na na na na na na na na na na na na na Lambdaman!", loop.invoke("Lambdaman!"));
6163      * }</pre></blockquote>
6164      *
6165      * @apiNote Example with the simplest possible body method type,
6166      * and passing the number of iterations to the loop invocation:
6167      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
6168      * // String s = "Lambdaman!"; for (int i = 0; i < 13; ++i) { s = "na " + s; } return s;
6169      * // => a variation on a well known theme
6170      * static String step(String v, int counter ) { return "na " + v; }
6171      * // assume MH_step is a handle to the method above
6172      * MethodHandle count = MethodHandles.dropArguments(MethodHandles.identity(int.class), 1, String.class);
6173      * MethodHandle start = MethodHandles.dropArguments(MethodHandles.identity(String.class), 0, int.class);
6174      * MethodHandle loop = MethodHandles.countedLoop(count, start, MH_step);  // (v, i) -> "na " + v
6175      * assertEquals("na na na na na na na na na na na na na Lambdaman!", loop.invoke(13, "Lambdaman!"));
6176      * }</pre></blockquote>
6177      *
6178      * @apiNote Example that treats the number of iterations, string to append to, and string to append
6179      * as loop parameters:
6180      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
6181      * // String s = "Lambdaman!", t = "na"; for (int i = 0; i < 13; ++i) { s = t + " " + s; } return s;
6182      * // => a variation on a well known theme
6183      * static String step(String v, int counter, int iterations_, String pre, String start_) { return pre + " " + v; }
6184      * // assume MH_step is a handle to the method above
6185      * MethodHandle count = MethodHandles.identity(int.class);
6186      * MethodHandle start = MethodHandles.dropArguments(MethodHandles.identity(String.class), 0, int.class, String.class);
6187      * MethodHandle loop = MethodHandles.countedLoop(count, start, MH_step);  // (v, i, _, pre, _) -> pre + " " + v
6188      * assertEquals("na na na na na na na na na na na na na Lambdaman!", loop.invoke(13, "na", "Lambdaman!"));
6189      * }</pre></blockquote>
6190      *
6191      * @apiNote Example that illustrates the usage of {@link #dropArgumentsToMatch(MethodHandle, int, List, int)}
6192      * to enforce a loop type:
6193      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
6194      * // String s = "Lambdaman!", t = "na"; for (int i = 0; i < 13; ++i) { s = t + " " + s; } return s;
6195      * // => a variation on a well known theme
6196      * static String step(String v, int counter, String pre) { return pre + " " + v; }
6197      * // assume MH_step is a handle to the method above
6198      * MethodType loopType = methodType(String.class, String.class, int.class, String.class);
6199      * MethodHandle count = MethodHandles.dropArgumentsToMatch(MethodHandles.identity(int.class),    0, loopType.parameterList(), 1);
6200      * MethodHandle start = MethodHandles.dropArgumentsToMatch(MethodHandles.identity(String.class), 0, loopType.parameterList(), 2);
6201      * MethodHandle body  = MethodHandles.dropArgumentsToMatch(MH_step,                              2, loopType.parameterList(), 0);
6202      * MethodHandle loop = MethodHandles.countedLoop(count, start, body);  // (v, i, pre, _, _) -> pre + " " + v
6203      * assertEquals("na na na na na na na na na na na na na Lambdaman!", loop.invoke("na", 13, "Lambdaman!"));
6204      * }</pre></blockquote>
6205      *
6206      * @apiNote The implementation of this method can be expressed as follows:
6207      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
6208      * MethodHandle countedLoop(MethodHandle iterations, MethodHandle init, MethodHandle body) {
6209      *     return countedLoop(empty(iterations.type()), iterations, init, body);
6210      * }
6211      * }</pre></blockquote>
6212      *
6213      * @param iterations a non-{@code null} handle to return the number of iterations this loop should run. The handle's
6214      *                   result type must be {@code int}. See above for other constraints.
6215      * @param init optional initializer, providing the initial value of the loop variable.
6216      *             May be {@code null}, implying a default initial value.  See above for other constraints.
6217      * @param body body of the loop, which may not be {@code null}.
6218      *             It controls the loop parameters and result type in the standard case (see above for details).
6219      *             It must accept its own return type (if non-void) plus an {@code int} parameter (for the counter),
6220      *             and may accept any number of additional types.
6221      *             See above for other constraints.
6222      *
6223      * @return a method handle representing the loop.
6224      * @throws NullPointerException if either of the {@code iterations} or {@code body} handles is {@code null}.
6225      * @throws IllegalArgumentException if any argument violates the rules formulated above.
6226      *
6227      * @see #countedLoop(MethodHandle, MethodHandle, MethodHandle, MethodHandle)
6228      * @since 9
6229      */
6230     public static MethodHandle countedLoop(MethodHandle iterations, MethodHandle init, MethodHandle body) {
6231         return countedLoop(empty(iterations.type()), iterations, init, body);
6232     }
6233 
6234     /**
6235      * Constructs a loop that counts over a range of numbers.
6236      * This is a convenience wrapper for the {@linkplain #loop(MethodHandle[][]) generic loop combinator}.
6237      * <p>
6238      * The loop counter {@code i} is a loop iteration variable of type {@code int}.
6239      * The {@code start} and {@code end} handles determine the start (inclusive) and end (exclusive)
6240      * values of the loop counter.
6241      * The loop counter will be initialized to the {@code int} value returned from the evaluation of the
6242      * {@code start} handle and run to the value returned from {@code end} (exclusively) with a step width of 1.
6243      * <p>
6244      * If the {@code body} handle returns a non-{@code void} type {@code V}, a leading loop iteration variable
6245      * of that type is also present.  This variable is initialized using the optional {@code init} handle,
6246      * or to the {@linkplain #empty default value} of type {@code V} if that handle is {@code null}.
6247      * <p>
6248      * In each iteration, the iteration variables are passed to an invocation of the {@code body} handle.
6249      * A non-{@code void} value returned from the body (of type {@code V}) updates the leading
6250      * iteration variable.
6251      * The result of the loop handle execution will be the final {@code V} value of that variable
6252      * (or {@code void} if there is no {@code V} variable).
6253      * <p>
6254      * The following rules hold for the argument handles:<ul>
6255      * <li>The {@code start} and {@code end} handles must not be {@code null}, and must both return
6256      * the common type {@code int}, referred to here as {@code I} in parameter type lists.
6257      * <li>The {@code body} handle must not be {@code null}; its type must be of the form
6258      * {@code (V I A...)V}, where {@code V} is non-{@code void}, or else {@code (I A...)void}.
6259      * (In the {@code void} case, we assign the type {@code void} to the name {@code V},
6260      * and we will write {@code (V I A...)V} with the understanding that a {@code void} type {@code V}
6261      * is quietly dropped from the parameter list, leaving {@code (I A...)V}.)
6262      * <li>The parameter list {@code (V I A...)} of the body contributes to a list
6263      * of types called the <em>internal parameter list</em>.
6264      * It will constrain the parameter lists of the other loop parts.
6265      * <li>As a special case, if the body contributes only {@code V} and {@code I} types,
6266      * with no additional {@code A} types, then the internal parameter list is extended by
