6267      * the argument types {@code A...} of the {@code end} handle.
6268      * <li>If the iteration variable types {@code (V I)} are dropped from the internal parameter list, the resulting shorter
6269      * list {@code (A...)} is called the <em>external parameter list</em>.
6270      * <li>The body return type {@code V}, if non-{@code void}, determines the type of an
6271      * additional state variable of the loop.
6272      * The body must both accept a leading parameter and return a value of this type {@code V}.
6273      * <li>If {@code init} is non-{@code null}, it must have return type {@code V}.
6274      * Its parameter list (of some <a href="MethodHandles.html#astar">form {@code (A*)}</a>) must be
6275      * <a href="MethodHandles.html#effid">effectively identical</a>
6276      * to the external parameter list {@code (A...)}.
6277      * <li>If {@code init} is {@code null}, the loop variable will be initialized to its
6278      * {@linkplain #empty default value}.
6279      * <li>The parameter list of {@code start} (of some form {@code (A*)}) must be
6280      * effectively identical to the external parameter list {@code (A...)}.
6281      * <li>Likewise, the parameter list of {@code end} must be effectively identical
6282      * to the external parameter list.
6283      * </ul>
6284      * <p>
6285      * The resulting loop handle's result type and parameter signature are determined as follows:<ul>
6286      * <li>The loop handle's result type is the result type {@code V} of the body.
6287      * <li>The loop handle's parameter types are the types {@code (A...)},
6288      * from the external parameter list.
6289      * </ul>
6290      * <p>
6291      * Here is pseudocode for the resulting loop handle. In the code, {@code V}/{@code v} represent the type / value of
6292      * the second loop variable as well as the result type of the loop; and {@code A...}/{@code a...} represent
6293      * arguments passed to the loop.
6294      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
6295      * int start(A...);
6296      * int end(A...);
6297      * V init(A...);
6298      * V body(V, int, A...);
6299      * V countedLoop(A... a...) {
6300      *   int e = end(a...);
6301      *   int s = start(a...);
6302      *   V v = init(a...);
6303      *   for (int i = s; i < e; ++i) {
6304      *     v = body(v, i, a...);
6305      *   }
6306      *   return v;
6307      * }
6308      * }</pre></blockquote>
6309      *
6310      * @apiNote The implementation of this method can be expressed as follows:
6311      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
6312      * MethodHandle countedLoop(MethodHandle start, MethodHandle end, MethodHandle init, MethodHandle body) {
6313      *     MethodHandle returnVar = dropArguments(identity(init.type().returnType()), 0, int.class, int.class);
6314      *     // assume MH_increment and MH_predicate are handles to implementation-internal methods with
6315      *     // the following semantics:
6316      *     // MH_increment: (int limit, int counter) -> counter + 1
6317      *     // MH_predicate: (int limit, int counter) -> counter < limit
6318      *     Class<?> counterType = start.type().returnType();  // int
6319      *     Class<?> returnType = body.type().returnType();
6320      *     MethodHandle incr = MH_increment, pred = MH_predicate, retv = null;
6321      *     if (returnType != void.class) {  // ignore the V variable
6322      *         incr = dropArguments(incr, 1, returnType);  // (limit, v, i) => (limit, i)
6323      *         pred = dropArguments(pred, 1, returnType);  // ditto
6324      *         retv = dropArguments(identity(returnType), 0, counterType); // ignore limit
6325      *     }
6326      *     body = dropArguments(body, 0, counterType);  // ignore the limit variable
6327      *     MethodHandle[]
6328      *         loopLimit  = { end, null, pred, retv }, // limit = end(); i < limit || return v
6329      *         bodyClause = { init, body },            // v = init(); v = body(v, i)
6330      *         indexVar   = { start, incr };           // i = start(); i = i + 1
6331      *     return loop(loopLimit, bodyClause, indexVar);
6332      * }
6333      * }</pre></blockquote>
6334      *
6335      * @param start a non-{@code null} handle to return the start value of the loop counter, which must be {@code int}.
6336      *              See above for other constraints.
6337      * @param end a non-{@code null} handle to return the end value of the loop counter (the loop will run to
6338      *            {@code end-1}). The result type must be {@code int}. See above for other constraints.
6339      * @param init optional initializer, providing the initial value of the loop variable.
6340      *             May be {@code null}, implying a default initial value.  See above for other constraints.
6341      * @param body body of the loop, which may not be {@code null}.
6342      *             It controls the loop parameters and result type in the standard case (see above for details).
6343      *             It must accept its own return type (if non-void) plus an {@code int} parameter (for the counter),
6344      *             and may accept any number of additional types.
6345      *             See above for other constraints.
6346      *
6347      * @return a method handle representing the loop.
6348      * @throws NullPointerException if any of the {@code start}, {@code end}, or {@code body} handles is {@code null}.
6349      * @throws IllegalArgumentException if any argument violates the rules formulated above.
6350      *
6351      * @see #countedLoop(MethodHandle, MethodHandle, MethodHandle)
6352      * @since 9
6353      */
6354     public static MethodHandle countedLoop(MethodHandle start, MethodHandle end, MethodHandle init, MethodHandle body) {
6355         countedLoopChecks(start, end, init, body);
6356         Class<?> counterType = start.type().returnType();  // int, but who's counting?
6357         Class<?> limitType   = end.type().returnType();    // yes, int again
6358         Class<?> returnType  = body.type().returnType();
6359         MethodHandle incr = MethodHandleImpl.getConstantHandle(MethodHandleImpl.MH_countedLoopStep);
6360         MethodHandle pred = MethodHandleImpl.getConstantHandle(MethodHandleImpl.MH_countedLoopPred);
6361         MethodHandle retv = null;
6362         if (returnType != void.class) {
6363             incr = dropArguments(incr, 1, returnType);  // (limit, v, i) => (limit, i)
6364             pred = dropArguments(pred, 1, returnType);  // ditto
6365             retv = dropArguments(identity(returnType), 0, counterType);
6366         }
6367         body = dropArguments(body, 0, counterType);  // ignore the limit variable
6368         MethodHandle[]
6369             loopLimit  = { end, null, pred, retv }, // limit = end(); i < limit || return v
6370             bodyClause = { init, body },            // v = init(); v = body(v, i)
6371             indexVar   = { start, incr };           // i = start(); i = i + 1
6372         return loop(loopLimit, bodyClause, indexVar);
6373     }
6374 
6375     private static void countedLoopChecks(MethodHandle start, MethodHandle end, MethodHandle init, MethodHandle body) {
6376         Objects.requireNonNull(start);
6377         Objects.requireNonNull(end);
6378         Objects.requireNonNull(body);
6379         Class<?> counterType = start.type().returnType();
6380         if (counterType != int.class) {
6381             MethodType expected = start.type().changeReturnType(int.class);
6382             throw misMatchedTypes("start function", start.type(), expected);
6383         } else if (end.type().returnType() != counterType) {
6384             MethodType expected = end.type().changeReturnType(counterType);
6385             throw misMatchedTypes("end function", end.type(), expected);
6386         }
6387         MethodType bodyType = body.type();
6388         Class<?> returnType = bodyType.returnType();
6389         List<Class<?>> innerList = bodyType.parameterList();
6390         // strip leading V value if present
6391         int vsize = (returnType == void.class ? 0 : 1);
6392         if (vsize != 0 && (innerList.size() == 0 || innerList.get(0) != returnType)) {
6393             // argument list has no "V" => error
6394             MethodType expected = bodyType.insertParameterTypes(0, returnType);
6395             throw misMatchedTypes("body function", bodyType, expected);
6396         } else if (innerList.size() <= vsize || innerList.get(vsize) != counterType) {
6397             // missing I type => error
6398             MethodType expected = bodyType.insertParameterTypes(vsize, counterType);
6399             throw misMatchedTypes("body function", bodyType, expected);
6400         }
6401         List<Class<?>> outerList = innerList.subList(vsize + 1, innerList.size());
6402         if (outerList.isEmpty()) {
6403             // special case; take lists from end handle
6404             outerList = end.type().parameterList();
6405             innerList = bodyType.insertParameterTypes(vsize + 1, outerList).parameterList();
6406         }
6407         MethodType expected = methodType(counterType, outerList);
6408         if (!start.type().effectivelyIdenticalParameters(0, outerList)) {
6409             throw misMatchedTypes("start parameter types", start.type(), expected);
6410         }
6411         if (end.type() != start.type() &&
6412             !end.type().effectivelyIdenticalParameters(0, outerList)) {
6413             throw misMatchedTypes("end parameter types", end.type(), expected);
6414         }
6415         if (init != null) {
6416             MethodType initType = init.type();
6417             if (initType.returnType() != returnType ||
6418                 !initType.effectivelyIdenticalParameters(0, outerList)) {
6419                 throw misMatchedTypes("loop initializer", initType, methodType(returnType, outerList));
6420             }
6421         }
6422     }
6423 
6424     /**
6425      * Constructs a loop that ranges over the values produced by an {@code Iterator<T>}.
6426      * This is a convenience wrapper for the {@linkplain #loop(MethodHandle[][]) generic loop combinator}.
6427      * <p>
6428      * The iterator itself will be determined by the evaluation of the {@code iterator} handle.
6429      * Each value it produces will be stored in a loop iteration variable of type {@code T}.
6430      * <p>
6431      * If the {@code body} handle returns a non-{@code void} type {@code V}, a leading loop iteration variable
6432      * of that type is also present.  This variable is initialized using the optional {@code init} handle,
6433      * or to the {@linkplain #empty default value} of type {@code V} if that handle is {@code null}.
6434      * <p>
6435      * In each iteration, the iteration variables are passed to an invocation of the {@code body} handle.
6436      * A non-{@code void} value returned from the body (of type {@code V}) updates the leading
6437      * iteration variable.
6438      * The result of the loop handle execution will be the final {@code V} value of that variable
6439      * (or {@code void} if there is no {@code V} variable).
6440      * <p>
6441      * The following rules hold for the argument handles:<ul>
6442      * <li>The {@code body} handle must not be {@code null}; its type must be of the form
6443      * {@code (V T A...)V}, where {@code V} is non-{@code void}, or else {@code (T A...)void}.
6444      * (In the {@code void} case, we assign the type {@code void} to the name {@code V},
6445      * and we will write {@code (V T A...)V} with the understanding that a {@code void} type {@code V}
6446      * is quietly dropped from the parameter list, leaving {@code (T A...)V}.)
6447      * <li>The parameter list {@code (V T A...)} of the body contributes to a list
6448      * of types called the <em>internal parameter list</em>.
6449      * It will constrain the parameter lists of the other loop parts.
6450      * <li>As a special case, if the body contributes only {@code V} and {@code T} types,
6451      * with no additional {@code A} types, then the internal parameter list is extended by
6452      * the argument types {@code A...} of the {@code iterator} handle; if it is {@code null} the
6453      * single type {@code Iterable} is added and constitutes the {@code A...} list.
6454      * <li>If the iteration variable types {@code (V T)} are dropped from the internal parameter list, the resulting shorter
6455      * list {@code (A...)} is called the <em>external parameter list</em>.
6456      * <li>The body return type {@code V}, if non-{@code void}, determines the type of an
6457      * additional state variable of the loop.
6458      * The body must both accept a leading parameter and return a value of this type {@code V}.
6459      * <li>If {@code init} is non-{@code null}, it must have return type {@code V}.
6460      * Its parameter list (of some <a href="MethodHandles.html#astar">form {@code (A*)}</a>) must be
6461      * <a href="MethodHandles.html#effid">effectively identical</a>
6462      * to the external parameter list {@code (A...)}.
6463      * <li>If {@code init} is {@code null}, the loop variable will be initialized to its
6464      * {@linkplain #empty default value}.
6465      * <li>If the {@code iterator} handle is non-{@code null}, it must have the return
6466      * type {@code java.util.Iterator} or a subtype thereof.
6467      * The iterator it produces when the loop is executed will be assumed
6468      * to yield values which can be converted to type {@code T}.
6469      * <li>The parameter list of an {@code iterator} that is non-{@code null} (of some form {@code (A*)}) must be
6470      * effectively identical to the external parameter list {@code (A...)}.
6471      * <li>If {@code iterator} is {@code null} it defaults to a method handle which behaves
6472      * like {@link java.lang.Iterable#iterator()}.  In that case, the internal parameter list
6473      * {@code (V T A...)} must have at least one {@code A} type, and the default iterator
6474      * handle parameter is adjusted to accept the leading {@code A} type, as if by
6475      * the {@link MethodHandle#asType asType} conversion method.
6476      * The leading {@code A} type must be {@code Iterable} or a subtype thereof.
6477      * This conversion step, done at loop construction time, must not throw a {@code WrongMethodTypeException}.
6478      * </ul>
6479      * <p>
6480      * The type {@code T} may be either a primitive or reference.
6481      * Since type {@code Iterator<T>} is erased in the method handle representation to the raw type {@code Iterator},
6482      * the {@code iteratedLoop} combinator adjusts the leading argument type for {@code body} to {@code Object}
6483      * as if by the {@link MethodHandle#asType asType} conversion method.
6484      * Therefore, if an iterator of the wrong type appears as the loop is executed, runtime exceptions may occur
6485      * as the result of dynamic conversions performed by {@link MethodHandle#asType(MethodType)}.
6486      * <p>
6487      * The resulting loop handle's result type and parameter signature are determined as follows:<ul>
6488      * <li>The loop handle's result type is the result type {@code V} of the body.
6489      * <li>The loop handle's parameter types are the types {@code (A...)},
6490      * from the external parameter list.
6491      * </ul>
6492      * <p>
6493      * Here is pseudocode for the resulting loop handle. In the code, {@code V}/{@code v} represent the type / value of
6494      * the loop variable as well as the result type of the loop; {@code T}/{@code t}, that of the elements of the
6495      * structure the loop iterates over, and {@code A...}/{@code a...} represent arguments passed to the loop.
6496      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
6497      * Iterator<T> iterator(A...);  // defaults to Iterable::iterator
6498      * V init(A...);
6499      * V body(V,T,A...);
6500      * V iteratedLoop(A... a...) {
6501      *   Iterator<T> it = iterator(a...);
6502      *   V v = init(a...);
6503      *   while (it.hasNext()) {
6504      *     T t = it.next();
6505      *     v = body(v, t, a...);
6506      *   }
6507      *   return v;
6508      * }
6509      * }</pre></blockquote>
6510      *
6511      * @apiNote Example:
6512      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
6513      * // get an iterator from a list
6514      * static List<String> reverseStep(List<String> r, String e) {
6515      *   r.add(0, e);
6516      *   return r;
6517      * }
6518      * static List<String> newArrayList() { return new ArrayList<>(); }
6519      * // assume MH_reverseStep and MH_newArrayList are handles to the above methods
6520      * MethodHandle loop = MethodHandles.iteratedLoop(null, MH_newArrayList, MH_reverseStep);
6521      * List<String> list = Arrays.asList("a", "b", "c", "d", "e");
6522      * List<String> reversedList = Arrays.asList("e", "d", "c", "b", "a");
6523      * assertEquals(reversedList, (List<String>) loop.invoke(list));
6524      * }</pre></blockquote>
6525      *
6526      * @apiNote The implementation of this method can be expressed approximately as follows:
6527      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
6528      * MethodHandle iteratedLoop(MethodHandle iterator, MethodHandle init, MethodHandle body) {
6529      *     // assume MH_next, MH_hasNext, MH_startIter are handles to methods of Iterator/Iterable
6530      *     Class<?> returnType = body.type().returnType();
6531      *     Class<?> ttype = body.type().parameterType(returnType == void.class ? 0 : 1);
6532      *     MethodHandle nextVal = MH_next.asType(MH_next.type().changeReturnType(ttype));
6533      *     MethodHandle retv = null, step = body, startIter = iterator;
6534      *     if (returnType != void.class) {
6535      *         // the simple thing first:  in (I V A...), drop the I to get V
6536      *         retv = dropArguments(identity(returnType), 0, Iterator.class);
6537      *         // body type signature (V T A...), internal loop types (I V A...)
6538      *         step = swapArguments(body, 0, 1);  // swap V <-> T
6539      *     }
6540      *     if (startIter == null)  startIter = MH_getIter;
6541      *     MethodHandle[]
6542      *         iterVar    = { startIter, null, MH_hasNext, retv }, // it = iterator; while (it.hasNext())
6543      *         bodyClause = { init, filterArguments(step, 0, nextVal) };  // v = body(v, t, a)
6544      *     return loop(iterVar, bodyClause);
6545      * }
6546      * }</pre></blockquote>
6547      *
6548      * @param iterator an optional handle to return the iterator to start the loop.
6549      *                 If non-{@code null}, the handle must return {@link java.util.Iterator} or a subtype.
6550      *                 See above for other constraints.
6551      * @param init optional initializer, providing the initial value of the loop variable.
6552      *             May be {@code null}, implying a default initial value.  See above for other constraints.
6553      * @param body body of the loop, which may not be {@code null}.
6554      *             It controls the loop parameters and result type in the standard case (see above for details).
6555      *             It must accept its own return type (if non-void) plus a {@code T} parameter (for the iterated values),
6556      *             and may accept any number of additional types.
6557      *             See above for other constraints.
6558      *
6559      * @return a method handle embodying the iteration loop functionality.
6560      * @throws NullPointerException if the {@code body} handle is {@code null}.
6561      * @throws IllegalArgumentException if any argument violates the above requirements.
6562      *
6563      * @since 9
6564      */
6565     public static MethodHandle iteratedLoop(MethodHandle iterator, MethodHandle init, MethodHandle body) {
6566         Class<?> iterableType = iteratedLoopChecks(iterator, init, body);
6567         Class<?> returnType = body.type().returnType();
6568         MethodHandle hasNext = MethodHandleImpl.getConstantHandle(MethodHandleImpl.MH_iteratePred);
6569         MethodHandle nextRaw = MethodHandleImpl.getConstantHandle(MethodHandleImpl.MH_iterateNext);
6570         MethodHandle startIter;
6571         MethodHandle nextVal;
6572         {
6573             MethodType iteratorType;
6574             if (iterator == null) {
6575                 // derive argument type from body, if available, else use Iterable
6576                 startIter = MethodHandleImpl.getConstantHandle(MethodHandleImpl.MH_initIterator);
6577                 iteratorType = startIter.type().changeParameterType(0, iterableType);
6578             } else {
6579                 // force return type to the internal iterator class
6580                 iteratorType = iterator.type().changeReturnType(Iterator.class);
6581                 startIter = iterator;
6582             }
6583             Class<?> ttype = body.type().parameterType(returnType == void.class ? 0 : 1);
6584             MethodType nextValType = nextRaw.type().changeReturnType(ttype);
6585 
6586             // perform the asType transforms under an exception transformer, as per spec.:
6587             try {
6588                 startIter = startIter.asType(iteratorType);
6589                 nextVal = nextRaw.asType(nextValType);
6590             } catch (WrongMethodTypeException ex) {
6591                 throw new IllegalArgumentException(ex);
6592             }
6593         }
6594 
6595         MethodHandle retv = null, step = body;
6596         if (returnType != void.class) {
6597             // the simple thing first:  in (I V A...), drop the I to get V
6598             retv = dropArguments(identity(returnType), 0, Iterator.class);
6599             // body type signature (V T A...), internal loop types (I V A...)
6600             step = swapArguments(body, 0, 1);  // swap V <-> T
6601         }
6602 
6603         MethodHandle[]
6604             iterVar    = { startIter, null, hasNext, retv },
6605             bodyClause = { init, filterArgument(step, 0, nextVal) };
6606         return loop(iterVar, bodyClause);
6607     }
6608 
6609     private static Class<?> iteratedLoopChecks(MethodHandle iterator, MethodHandle init, MethodHandle body) {
6610         Objects.requireNonNull(body);
6611         MethodType bodyType = body.type();
6612         Class<?> returnType = bodyType.returnType();
6613         List<Class<?>> internalParamList = bodyType.parameterList();
6614         // strip leading V value if present
6615         int vsize = (returnType == void.class ? 0 : 1);
6616         if (vsize != 0 && (internalParamList.size() == 0 || internalParamList.get(0) != returnType)) {
6617             // argument list has no "V" => error
6618             MethodType expected = bodyType.insertParameterTypes(0, returnType);
6619             throw misMatchedTypes("body function", bodyType, expected);
6620         } else if (internalParamList.size() <= vsize) {
6621             // missing T type => error
6622             MethodType expected = bodyType.insertParameterTypes(vsize, Object.class);
6623             throw misMatchedTypes("body function", bodyType, expected);
6624         }
6625         List<Class<?>> externalParamList = internalParamList.subList(vsize + 1, internalParamList.size());
6626         Class<?> iterableType = null;
6627         if (iterator != null) {
6628             // special case; if the body handle only declares V and T then
6629             // the external parameter list is obtained from iterator handle
6630             if (externalParamList.isEmpty()) {
6631                 externalParamList = iterator.type().parameterList();
6632             }
6633             MethodType itype = iterator.type();
6634             if (!Iterator.class.isAssignableFrom(itype.returnType())) {
6635                 throw newIllegalArgumentException("iteratedLoop first argument must have Iterator return type");
6636             }
6637             if (!itype.effectivelyIdenticalParameters(0, externalParamList)) {
6638                 MethodType expected = methodType(itype.returnType(), externalParamList);
6639                 throw misMatchedTypes("iterator parameters", itype, expected);
6640             }
6641         } else {
6642             if (externalParamList.isEmpty()) {
6643                 // special case; if the iterator handle is null and the body handle
6644                 // only declares V and T then the external parameter list consists
6645                 // of Iterable
6646                 externalParamList = Arrays.asList(Iterable.class);
6647                 iterableType = Iterable.class;
6648             } else {
6649                 // special case; if the iterator handle is null and the external
6650                 // parameter list is not empty then the first parameter must be
6651                 // assignable to Iterable
6652                 iterableType = externalParamList.get(0);
6653                 if (!Iterable.class.isAssignableFrom(iterableType)) {
6654                     throw newIllegalArgumentException(
6655                             "inferred first loop argument must inherit from Iterable: " + iterableType);
6656                 }
6657             }
6658         }
6659         if (init != null) {
6660             MethodType initType = init.type();
6661             if (initType.returnType() != returnType ||
6662                     !initType.effectivelyIdenticalParameters(0, externalParamList)) {
6663                 throw misMatchedTypes("loop initializer", initType, methodType(returnType, externalParamList));
6664             }
6665         }
6666         return iterableType;  // help the caller a bit
6667     }
6668 
6669     /*non-public*/
6670     static MethodHandle swapArguments(MethodHandle mh, int i, int j) {
6671         // there should be a better way to uncross my wires
6672         int arity = mh.type().parameterCount();
6673         int[] order = new int[arity];
6674         for (int k = 0; k < arity; k++)  order[k] = k;
6675         order[i] = j; order[j] = i;
6676         Class<?>[] types = mh.type().parameterArray();
6677         Class<?> ti = types[i]; types[i] = types[j]; types[j] = ti;
6678         MethodType swapType = methodType(mh.type().returnType(), types);
6679         return permuteArguments(mh, swapType, order);
6680     }
6681 
6682     /**
6683      * Makes a method handle that adapts a {@code target} method handle by wrapping it in a {@code try-finally} block.
6684      * Another method handle, {@code cleanup}, represents the functionality of the {@code finally} block. Any exception
6685      * thrown during the execution of the {@code target} handle will be passed to the {@code cleanup} handle. The
6686      * exception will be rethrown, unless {@code cleanup} handle throws an exception first.  The
6687      * value returned from the {@code cleanup} handle's execution will be the result of the execution of the
6688      * {@code try-finally} handle.
6689      * <p>
6690      * The {@code cleanup} handle will be passed one or two additional leading arguments.
6691      * The first is the exception thrown during the
6692      * execution of the {@code target} handle, or {@code null} if no exception was thrown.
6693      * The second is the result of the execution of the {@code target} handle, or, if it throws an exception,
6694      * a {@code null}, zero, or {@code false} value of the required type is supplied as a placeholder.
6695      * The second argument is not present if the {@code target} handle has a {@code void} return type.
6696      * (Note that, except for argument type conversions, combinators represent {@code void} values in parameter lists
6697      * by omitting the corresponding paradoxical arguments, not by inserting {@code null} or zero values.)
6698      * <p>
6699      * The {@code target} and {@code cleanup} handles must have the same corresponding argument and return types, except
6700      * that the {@code cleanup} handle may omit trailing arguments. Also, the {@code cleanup} handle must have one or
6701      * two extra leading parameters:<ul>
6702      * <li>a {@code Throwable}, which will carry the exception thrown by the {@code target} handle (if any); and
6703      * <li>a parameter of the same type as the return type of both {@code target} and {@code cleanup}, which will carry
6704      * the result from the execution of the {@code target} handle.
6705      * This parameter is not present if the {@code target} returns {@code void}.
6706      * </ul>
6707      * <p>
6708      * The pseudocode for the resulting adapter looks as follows. In the code, {@code V} represents the result type of
6709      * the {@code try/finally} construct; {@code A}/{@code a}, the types and values of arguments to the resulting
6710      * handle consumed by the cleanup; and {@code B}/{@code b}, those of arguments to the resulting handle discarded by
6711      * the cleanup.
6712      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
6713      * V target(A..., B...);
6714      * V cleanup(Throwable, V, A...);
6715      * V adapter(A... a, B... b) {
6716      *   V result = (zero value for V);
6717      *   Throwable throwable = null;
6718      *   try {
6719      *     result = target(a..., b...);
6720      *   } catch (Throwable t) {
6721      *     throwable = t;
6722      *     throw t;
6723      *   } finally {
6724      *     result = cleanup(throwable, result, a...);
6725      *   }
6726      *   return result;
6727      * }
6728      * }</pre></blockquote>
6729      * <p>
6730      * Note that the saved arguments ({@code a...} in the pseudocode) cannot
6731      * be modified by execution of the target, and so are passed unchanged
6732      * from the caller to the cleanup, if it is invoked.
6733      * <p>
6734      * The target and cleanup must return the same type, even if the cleanup
6735      * always throws.
6736      * To create such a throwing cleanup, compose the cleanup logic
6737      * with {@link #throwException throwException},
6738      * in order to create a method handle of the correct return type.
6739      * <p>
6740      * Note that {@code tryFinally} never converts exceptions into normal returns.
6741      * In rare cases where exceptions must be converted in that way, first wrap
6742      * the target with {@link #catchException(MethodHandle, Class, MethodHandle)}
6743      * to capture an outgoing exception, and then wrap with {@code tryFinally}.
6744      * <p>
6745      * It is recommended that the first parameter type of {@code cleanup} be
6746      * declared {@code Throwable} rather than a narrower subtype.  This ensures
6747      * {@code cleanup} will always be invoked with whatever exception that
6748      * {@code target} throws.  Declaring a narrower type may result in a
6749      * {@code ClassCastException} being thrown by the {@code try-finally}
6750      * handle if the type of the exception thrown by {@code target} is not
6751      * assignable to the first parameter type of {@code cleanup}.  Note that
6752      * various exception types of {@code VirtualMachineError},
6753      * {@code LinkageError}, and {@code RuntimeException} can in principle be
6754      * thrown by almost any kind of Java code, and a finally clause that
6755      * catches (say) only {@code IOException} would mask any of the others
6756      * behind a {@code ClassCastException}.
6757      *
6758      * @param target the handle whose execution is to be wrapped in a {@code try} block.
6759      * @param cleanup the handle that is invoked in the finally block.
6760      *
6761      * @return a method handle embodying the {@code try-finally} block composed of the two arguments.
6762      * @throws NullPointerException if any argument is null
6763      * @throws IllegalArgumentException if {@code cleanup} does not accept
6764      *          the required leading arguments, or if the method handle types do
6765      *          not match in their return types and their
6766      *          corresponding trailing parameters
6767      *
6768      * @see MethodHandles#catchException(MethodHandle, Class, MethodHandle)
6769      * @since 9
6770      */
6771     public static MethodHandle tryFinally(MethodHandle target, MethodHandle cleanup) {
6772         List<Class<?>> targetParamTypes = target.type().parameterList();
6773         Class<?> rtype = target.type().returnType();
6774 
6775         tryFinallyChecks(target, cleanup);
6776 
6777         // Match parameter lists: if the cleanup has a shorter parameter list than the target, add ignored arguments.
6778         // The cleanup parameter list (minus the leading Throwable and result parameters) must be a sublist of the
6779         // target parameter list.
6780         cleanup = dropArgumentsToMatch(cleanup, (rtype == void.class ? 1 : 2), targetParamTypes, 0);
6781 
6782         // Ensure that the intrinsic type checks the instance thrown by the
6783         // target against the first parameter of cleanup
6784         cleanup = cleanup.asType(cleanup.type().changeParameterType(0, Throwable.class));
6785 
6786         // Use asFixedArity() to avoid unnecessary boxing of last argument for VarargsCollector case.
6787         return MethodHandleImpl.makeTryFinally(target.asFixedArity(), cleanup.asFixedArity(), rtype, targetParamTypes);
6788     }
6789 
6790     private static void tryFinallyChecks(MethodHandle target, MethodHandle cleanup) {
6791         Class<?> rtype = target.type().returnType();
6792         if (rtype != cleanup.type().returnType()) {
6793             throw misMatchedTypes("target and return types", cleanup.type().returnType(), rtype);
6794         }
6795         MethodType cleanupType = cleanup.type();
6796         if (!Throwable.class.isAssignableFrom(cleanupType.parameterType(0))) {
6797             throw misMatchedTypes("cleanup first argument and Throwable", cleanup.type(), Throwable.class);
6798         }
6799         if (rtype != void.class && cleanupType.parameterType(1) != rtype) {
6800             throw misMatchedTypes("cleanup second argument and target return type", cleanup.type(), rtype);
6801         }
6802         // The cleanup parameter list (minus the leading Throwable and result parameters) must be a sublist of the
6803         // target parameter list.
6804         int cleanupArgIndex = rtype == void.class ? 1 : 2;
6805         if (!cleanupType.effectivelyIdenticalParameters(cleanupArgIndex, target.type().parameterList())) {
6806             throw misMatchedTypes("cleanup parameters after (Throwable,result) and target parameter list prefix",
6807                     cleanup.type(), target.type());
6808         }
6809     }
6810 
6811 }
